**Summary.** This paper studies how long-range interactions applied through non-unitary evolution change the phase diagram of Gaussian states. It demonstrates that the range of the interaction (alpha) dictates whether the system undergoes smooth crossovers or immediate transitions to topological or critical phases. The study uses analytical tools to show that even very long-range interactions do not necessarily induce sharp phase transitions at finite deformation strength.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides deep insights into how non-unitary dynamics and long-range interactions can bypass 1D constraints to induce phase transitions and change universality classes, which is highly relevant to many-body dynamics and non-equilibrium physics.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating how long-range deformations via non-unitary imaginary-time evolution affect the phase structure, entanglement scaling, and topological properties of Gaussian quantum states.

**Main result.** The decay exponent alpha of the long-range interactions determines the system's infrared behavior, identifying three regimes: smooth crossovers (alpha > 1), immediate topological transitions (alpha = 1), and instantaneous critical-like behavior (alpha < 1).

**Method.** Analytical approach using the Gaussian nature of the state, Bogoliubov transformations, Toeplitz matrix formalism (Fisher-Hartwig and Szego theorems), and complex contour integration.

**Model / system.** A 1D Majorana fermion chain (equivalent to the transverse field Ising model) undergoing non-unitary evolution generated by a quadratic Hamiltonian with power-law couplings (1/r^alpha).

**Key observables.** Entanglement entropy (Rényi and von Neumann), correlation functions (x-correlator, y-correlator, and string correlator), winding number, and effective central charge.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Decay exponent alpha, deformation strength beta, anisotropy gamma, magnetic field h, and chemical potential mu.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The system is assumed to be in a Gaussian/free-fermion state, and the analysis focuses on the odd-parity sector with periodic boundary conditions.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows a phase diagram of transitions as a function of beta and alpha; Figure 2 illustrates contour integration sectors; Figure 3 shows analytical decay of effective central charge; Figure 4 shows entanglement scaling; Figure 13 shows the evolution of the correlator symbol in the complex plane.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the non-unitary deformation protocol, defines the long-range Hamiltonian models, develops the analytical framework for the correlation matrix and symbol, analyzes the three distinct regimes based on alpha, and discusses emergent symmetries and topological diagnostics.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Imaginary-time evolution by a local Hamiltonian cannot induce a phase transition in one dimension, but longer-range interactions may subvert such constraints. Starting from the ground state of the Kitaev Majorana chain, we modify the wave function by an imaginary-time evolution generated by a quadratic Hamiltonian with power-law couplings that enhance pairing correlations, typically of the form $1/r^α$, where $r$ is the distance between two sites. As the state remains Gaussian, entanglement and correlation functions can be computed analytically. We find that the decay exponent $α$ controls three distinct infrared regimes: for $α>1$, the deformation produces only smooth crossovers at finite deformation strength, while the topological regime is reached only asymptotically as the deformation strength tends to infinity. At $α=1$, the deformation induces an immediate flow to the topological phase: an infinitesimal deformation strength drives the system to a topological regime, and in a particular case, an emergent Kramers-Wannier symmetry enforces Ising-like scaling at long distances. For $α<1$, the deformed state shows the same critical-like behavior for all non-zero deformation strength. We observe that even with arbitrarily long-range interactions, these models do not display a sharp phase transition at non-zero deformation strength.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2605.26818"></a>
### [Nonclassical energy-change distribution as a witness of non-Markovian quantum dynamics](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.26818v1)

**Authors:** Marco Pezzutto, Anton Corr, Gabriele De Chiara, Salvatore Lorenzo, Stefano Gherardini

**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `quantum measurements` **4/5** · `entanglement & information structure` **3/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **3/5** · `correlated / nonlocal dissipation` **2/5** · `methods for driven-dissipative` **2/5**

**Summary.** This paper demonstrates that the non-classicality (non-positivity) of the energy-change Kirkwood-Dirac distribution serves as a robust witness for non-Markovian quantum dynamics. It shows that this witness is particularly effective when system-environment interactions preserve energy and remains valid even under anisotropic coupling.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides a practical, measurement-efficient way to detect memory effects in open quantum systems using only local energy measurements, which is highly relevant for experimentalists in quantum optics and superconducting circuits.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper aims to identify non-Markovian quantum dynamics in open systems using only energy measurements by investigating the non-positivity of the energy-change Kirkwood-Dirac quasiprobability distribution.

**Main result.** Violations of CP-divisibility are always witnessed by non-positive values in the energy-change Kirkwood-Dirac distribution, a link that is strongest in energy-preserving interaction regimes.

**Method.** The authors use a collision model framework, applying matrix-element representations of qubit maps and evaluating non-positivity functionals of the Kirkwood-Dirac distribution.

**Model / system.** A memory-mediated collision model consisting of a system (S), an auxiliary memory (M), and an environment (A), modeled as spin-1/2 particles interacting via Heisenberg-type exchange interactions.

**Key observables.** System energy changes (u_S), Kirkwood-Dirac quasiprobability distribution, quantum mutual information, and anomalous energy fluxes.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Coupling anisotropy (gamma), system-memory-environment frequencies, detuning (delta_omega), and collision number (n).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The system is initialized in a thermal state, and the dynamics are assumed to be phase-covariant (z-rotation symmetry) in certain parts of the analysis.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 compares the non-positivity functional with non-CP-divisibility measures and energy conditions; Figure 4 shows the dependence of non-Markovianity measures (I_LFS, I_RHP) on the coupling anisotropy parameter gamma.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of non-Markovianity detection, defines a collision model with Heisenberg interactions, develops the mathematical framework for phase-covariant maps and Kirkwood-Dirac distributions, analyzes the impact of anisotropy on the witness, and concludes with a comparison of different non-Markovianity measures.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

We address the problem of identifying non-Markovian quantum time evolutions of an open quantum system by only performing measurements of the system's energy. We demonstrate that violations of CP-divisibility are always witnessed by non-positive values of the energy-change Kirkwood-Dirac quasiprobability distribution associated with the system's Hamiltonian, evaluated at consecutive times. The link between non CP-divisibility and non-positivity of the system's energy-change distribution is stronger when the system-environment interactions are energy-preserving. The witness works whenever anomalous energy fluxes, due to non-Markovianity, are realized. Anomalous fluxes are also detected by the non-Markovianity measure built over the quantum mutual information between the states of the open system and of a quantum correlated reference.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

**Summary.** This study demonstrates that combining microwave-driven Floquet engineering with Fano interference in a ring-chord quantum dot structure can significantly boost thermoelectric efficiency and spin-dependent transport. By using geometry to suppress thermal conductance while using microwaves to tune energy-selective channels, the authors achieve remarkably high figures of merit. This provides a strategy for designing high-performance nanoscale heat engines and spin filters.

**Why it may be interesting.** The paper explores the dynamic control of quantum interference and energy-selective transport using periodic driving, which is highly relevant to the study of open quantum systems and Floquet engineering of many-body states.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating how the interplay between microwave-driven Floquet sidebands and geometry-driven Fano interference can be used to enhance the thermoelectric and spin-caloritronic performance of multi-quantum-dot nanostructures.

**Main result.** The ring-chord geometry under microwave driving achieves an exceptional thermoelectric figure of merit ZT approx 12 and a spin figure of merit ZsT approx 18, reaching nearly 62% of the Carnot efficiency.

**Method.** Nonequilibrium Green's function (NEGF) formalism combined with Floquet theory and a self-consistent Hartree treatment of electron-electron interactions.

**Model / system.** A four-quantum-dot nanostructure in two geometries (pure ring and ring-chord) coupled to ferromagnetic leads, featuring on-site Coulomb interaction, Zeeman splitting, and time-periodic microwave driving.

**Key observables.** Electrical conductance, thermopower (Seebeck coefficient), electronic thermal conductance, spin-dependent transport, thermoelectric figures of merit (ZT and ZsT), and efficiency at maximum power.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Microwave amplitude, frequency, temperature, dot-lead coupling strength, spin polarization, and Zeeman splitting.

**Assumptions / limitations.** Wide-band approximation for lead self-energies, linear response regime, and neglect of phonon heat transport.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the schematic of ring and ring-chord geometries; Figures 3-4 plot conductance, thermal conductance, and Seebeck coefficient vs. energy; Figures 5-8 show temperature and power-efficiency trade-off dependencies; Figures 9-12 illustrate spin-dependent conductance, thermopurity, and parameter space contour plots.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the system geometry, details the Floquet-NEGF theoretical framework, compares transport in pure ring vs. ring-chord geometries, analyzes the impact of microwave driving on thermoelectric efficiency, and concludes with a study of spin-caloritronic performance under magnetic fields.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

We investigate photon-assisted thermoelectric transport in four--quantum-dot nanostructures featuring ring and ring--chord geometries coupled to ferromagnetic leads. Focusing on the interplay between microwave-induced Floquet sidebands and geometry-driven Fano interference, we employ the nonequilibrium Green's function formalism combined with Floquet theory and a self-consistent Hartree treatment of electron-electron interactions within the linear response regime. The inclusion of a longitudinal interdot chord bridging the lead-coupled dots introduces a discrete interference pathway that competes with the continuum of ring-mediated states, giving rise to pronounced Fano resonances. Microwave irradiation dynamically reshapes these resonances through photon absorption and emission processes, enabling tunable control of electrical conductance, thermopower, and electronic thermal conductance. Quantitatively, at an intermediate temperature of $T=0.3Γ_0$ (where $Γ_0$ denotes the dot-lead coupling strength), the microwave-driven ring-chord geometry exhibits an exceptional thermoelectric figure of merit of ZT $\approx$ 12 and an optimal efficiency--power trade-off, reaching nearly $62\%$ of the Carnot efficiency with an output power of $6.24~\mathrm{fW}$. Crucially, the combination of spin-polarized injection from the leads and Zeeman splitting within the dots induces a robust spin-dependence within this Floquet--Fano interference. This cooperative interplay results in an enhanced spin Seebeck response and a maximum spin thermoelectric figure of merit of nearly $Z_sT \approx 18$. Our findings establish microwave-driven engineering of Fano interference as an effective strategy for modulating spin-caloritronic behavior in multi-quantum-dot devices.

</details>

### [Statistical and Algorithmic Foundations of Probing Quantum Systems with Compressive Measurements: A Review](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.27191v1)

**Authors:** Zhen Qin, Michael B. Wakin, Zhihui Zhu  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.27191v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `quantum measurements` **4/5** · `entanglement & information structure` **3/5** · `analog quantum simulation` **2/5** · `measurement-induced transitions` **2/5** · `methods for driven-dissipative` **2/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">

<figure class="paper-figure-card">

<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 2.</b> Figure 2: Illustration of the PEPO from each element of the density matrix is illustrated in a diagrammatic form, where the line connecting two circles signifies the tensor contraction operation [96], and unconnected line segments denote indices.</figcaption>

**Summary.** This review provides a unified perspective on performing quantum state tomography on large-scale systems by exploiting structural priors. It connects the theory of measurement design and optimization algorithms to the field of compressed sensing, showing how to reduce the complexity of state reconstruction from exponential to polynomial scaling.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides a comprehensive theoretical bridge between signal processing (compressive sensing) and quantum information, offering scalable strategies for characterizing many-body dynamics and large-scale quantum devices.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The exponential scaling of Quantum State Tomography (QST) makes reconstructing general quantum states computationally and statistically impossible for large systems, necessitating methods that exploit inherent state structures.

**Main result.** The review establishes a unified framework for QST by connecting compact state representations, measurement design, and reconstruction algorithms, demonstrating that QST can be treated as a structured inverse problem.

**Method.** The paper surveys various approaches including compressive sensing, randomized measurements (Haar-random, t-designs, and classical shadows), and optimization-based reconstruction (convex relaxations and non-convex methods).

**Model / system.** The review focuses on large-scale quantum processors, programmable simulators, and error-corrected computers, specifically targeting structured states such as low-rank, tensor-network (MPS, MPO, PEPO), and neural quantum states.

**Key observables.** Fidelities, expectation values of Pauli observables, trace distance, and entanglement measures.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Hilbert-space dimension (d), number of measurement shots (M), number of POVMs (Q), and intrinsic dimension/complexity of the state.

**Assumptions / limitations.** Assumes the existence of underlying structure (e.g., low-rankness or tensor-network compressibility) and focuses on the statistical error from finite-shot measurements rather than hardware-specific noise.

**Paper structure.** The paper is organized around three interconnected themes: compact state representations, measurement design, and computational algorithms, framing QST as a structured inverse problem.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Quantum state tomography (QST) is a fundamental task in quantum information science that aims to reconstruct unknown quantum states from measurement data. However, the exponential growth of Hilbert-space dimension with system size makes full tomography of general quantum states statistically and computationally prohibitive. This challenge has motivated extensive research on structured quantum state tomography, where prior structure, such as low-rankness, tensor-network representations, shallow quantum circuits, and neural quantum states, can substantially reduce the effective degrees of freedom and enable scalable recovery. In this review, we provide a unified perspective on QST for structured quantum states through three closely related themes: compact state representations, measurement design, and computational algorithms. After reviewing common models for structured quantum states, we survey existing work on geometric preservation properties of measurement frameworks, ranging from informationally complete POVMs to randomized measurements, and their implications for sample complexity. On the algorithmic side, we review optimization methods for reconstructing structured quantum states from empirical measurements. By connecting QST with broader principles from compressive sensing, matrix sensing, and structured inverse problems, this survey highlights common theoretical foundations underlying sample complexity, measurement efficiency, and scalable recovery.

</details>

**Summary.** Researchers have successfully integrated two independently tunable squeezed-light sources on a single thin-film lithium niobate chip. By interfering these sources, they demonstrated the generation of continuous-variable entanglement. This provides a scalable pathway for building complex, integrated quantum photonic circuits.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work is highly relevant to quantum optics and quantum information as it demonstrates a scalable hardware building block for continuous-variable quantum computing and large-scale Gaussian photonic circuits.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The need for scalable, integrated, and independently controllable nonclassical light sources on a single platform for continuous-variable quantum information processing.

**Main result.** Demonstration of two indistinguishable and independently tunable optical parametric oscillators (OPOs) on a single thin-film lithium niobate (TFLN) chip, used to generate EPR-type two-mode entanglement.

**Method.** Fabrication of TFLN waveguides with periodic poling, use of on-chip micro-heaters for resonance tuning, and interference of the two squeezed modes on an off-chip beam splitter followed by balanced homodyne detection.

**Model / system.** An integrated photonic platform based on X-cut thin-film lithium niobate (TFLN) on SiO2, featuring two single-resonant OPOs utilizing spontaneous parametric down-conversion at telecom wavelengths (1550 nm).

**Key observables.** Squeezing levels (dB), Duan-Simon inseparability criterion value, quadrature variances, and OPO pump power thresholds.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Signal wavelength ~1550 nm, pump wavelength ~775 nm, squeezing up to 0.5 dB, total efficiency ~0.53-0.54, and OPO thresholds between 15-23 W.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The system operates in the low-pump regime well below the OPO threshold.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the device schematic and experimental setup; Figure 2 displays the fabricated chip layout and SEM images of waveguides; Figure 3 presents the squeezing spectrum, power dependence, and quadrature variance measurements.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the scalability problem, describes the TFLN device architecture and fabrication, details the experimental tuning and entanglement generation setup, presents the measurement of squeezing and entanglement, and concludes with limitations and future directions.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Scalable generation of nonclassical light sources on an integrated platform is a key requirement for photonic quantum information processing. In particular, realizing multiple indistinguishable squeezed light sources on a single chip is an essential step toward continuous-variable quantum computing. Here, we demonstrate the fabrication of two indistinguishable and independently controllable optical parametric oscillators on a thin-film lithium niobate (TFLN) platform. The device design focuses on reproducibility, independent tunability, and compatibility with larger telecom-wavelength continuous-variable photonic circuits. We observe up to 0.5 dB of directly measured squeezing below the shot-noise level from each source. By interfering the two modes on a beam splitter, we generate an EPR-type two-mode squeezed state and verify continuous-variable entanglement through violation of the Duan-Simon inseparability criterion. This is the first demonstration of two independently tunable squeezed-light sources on a single TFLN chip and their use for generating continuous-variable entanglement.

</details>

### [Practical Tests and Witnesses of Fermionic non-Gaussianity](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.26218v1)

**Authors:** Tobias Haug, Xhek Turkeshi, Piotr Sierant  
**Type:** both · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.26218v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `QC/QI experiment` **4/5** · `entanglement & information structure` **3/5** · `quantum measurements` **3/5** · `Keldysh / 2PI / non-Gaussian methods` **2/5**

Noisy simulation assumes single-qubit depolarizing noise Λp = (1 −p)ρ + p I</figcaption>

**Summary.** This paper presents new, efficient protocols for detecting and quantifying non-Gaussianity in fermionic systems using both single-copy and two-copy measurement schemes. It introduces a noise-robust witness for mixed states and demonstrates the practical utility of these tools on a real quantum processor. The work establishes a fundamental link between non-Gaussianity and the complexity of generating pseudorandom fermionic states.

**Why it may be interesting.** This is highly relevant for many-body dynamics and quantum computing as it provides tools to certify non-trivial correlations and 'magic' resources in fermionic systems, which are harder to detect than standard entanglement or coherence.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Developing scalable and practical methods to detect, witness, and quantify fermionic non-Gaussianity, which is essential for benchmarking quantum devices and certifying fermionic magic resources.

**Main result.** The authors introduce efficient two-copy Bell measurement and single-copy protocols for estimating fermionic antiflatness (FAF), demonstrating improved scaling in qubit number and error tolerance, and showing that noise can both reduce and enhance non-Gaussianity.

**Method.** The study utilizes two-copy Bell measurements on pairs of states and a single-copy scheme based on commuting Majorana bilinear matchings, alongside a new purity-corrected FAF witness for mixed states.

**Model / system.** The system consists of n fermionic modes described by 2n Majorana operators, mapped to n qubits via the Jordan-Wigner transformation, and tested on the IQM Garnet quantum computer.

**Key observables.** Fermionic Antiflatness (FAF1), Gaussian fidelity (F_AF), purity-corrected FAF witness (W_FAF), and quadratic Fock-basis coherence (C2).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Number of qubits (n), distance to the Gaussian set (epsilon_G), noise parameter (p), and non-Gaussian gate angle (theta).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The single-copy protocol assumes the ability to implement Clifford circuits and Pauli measurements; the two-copy protocol assumes access to two copies of the quantum state.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the two estimation protocols; Figure 2 details the Bell-measurement readout; Figure 3 shows experimental results on IQM Garnet; Figure 4 illustrates the evolution of the witness under various noise models; Figure 5 depicts the three-copy convolution test.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of non-Gaussianity detection, develops new two-copy and single-copy estimation protocols, provides complexity analysis, introduces a robust witness for mixed states, validates results on a quantum computer, and explores the link to pseudorandomness and gate complexity.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Detecting when a quantum state leaves the efficiently simulable fermionic Gaussian regime is a central task for benchmarking quantum devices and certifying fermionic magic resources. We develop practical tests and witnesses based on fermionic antiflatness (FAF), a covariance-matrix-based measure of non-Gaussianity. For $n$-qubit states, we estimate FAF using two complementary protocols: two-copy Bell measurements and a single-copy scheme based on commuting matchings of Majorana bilinears. These yield testers that distinguish pure Gaussian states from states $ε$-far from the Gaussian set, using $O(n^2/ε^2)$ two-copy Bell measurements or $O(n^3/ε^4)$ single-copy measurements, improving the state of the art in the dependence on both $n$ and $ε$. For mixed states, we introduce a purity-corrected FAF witness that certifies non-Gaussianity and is highly robust to noise. With our witness, we demonstrate on the IQM quantum computer that noise can both reduce and enhance non-Gaussianity. Finally, by examining pseudo non-Gaussianity, we show that the cryptographic task of pseudorandom-state generation requires extensive fermionic non-Gaussianity. Together, these results provide experimentally accessible tools for detecting, witnessing, and quantifying non-Gaussian fermionic resources.

</details>

ZENITH performance (a) Numerical time evolution of P, computed as the average of the survival probabilities of the states |↑⟩, |↓⟩, and |+⟩, on an ensemble of eight randomly distributed dipolar interacting qutrits under FID (solid blue line) and with the stroboscopic implementation of ZENITH for values of JT = 2, 1, 0.5, 0.1, respectively. (b) Protection factor as a function of JT. The factor for the protocol with JT = 0.1 is estimated to be Q ∼...</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.26863_figures/2605.26863_fig4.jpg" alt="Figure 4">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 4.</b> Figure 3(d) displays stroboscopic evolution on a cluster of eight NVs targeting a DC signal of strength µ = 0.1/T, both for FID and with ZENITH initiated on the optimal measurement state, considering two different experimentally relevant NV ensemble concentrations. While for FID dipolar coupling induces a fast decay of the signal, thereby preventing frequency estimation, the large coherence time availed by ZENITH yields clean oscillation from which the original DC signal can be reconstructed. Note that, as we show in Sec. VI of the SM [46], the optimal initial state can be achieved with a single pulse, and therefore does not introduce additional errors, nor it reduces the experiment time...</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** The paper introduces the ZENITH protocol, a new pulse sequence designed to eliminate dipolar interactions in NV center ensembles at zero magnetic field. By using universal qutrit control, the method significantly extends coherence times and enables high-sensitivity DC magnetometry. This advancement is crucial for quantum technologies operating in environments where external magnetic fields cannot be applied.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides a general framework for controlling interacting degenerate multilevel systems (qutrits) and offers a method to suppress many-body interactions without external bias fields, which is highly relevant to open quantum systems and quantum sensing.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The decoherence of dense Nitrogen-Vacancy (NV) center ensembles in diamond caused by dipolar interactions, especially in the absence of a bias magnetic field which is usually required to lift degeneracy.

**Main result.** The development of the ZENITH protocol, an 11-pulse sequence that achieves full dipolar decoupling at zero field, providing over two orders of magnitude improvement in coherence time and enabling enhanced DC magnetometry.

**Method.** The authors use Average Hamiltonian Theory and a group-theoretical Cayley graph approach to design a pulse sequence that cancels both energy-conserving and non-energy-conserving dipolar terms via universal qutrit control.

**Model / system.** Ensembles of Nitrogen-Vacancy (NV) centers in diamond, modeled as a spin-1 (qutrit) system with a V-degenerate ground state manifold subject to dipole-dipole interactions.

**Key observables.** Survival probability of qutrit coherent states, protection factor (coherence time ratio), and frequency estimation error for DC magnetometry.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Zero-field or low-bias magnetic field regime, dipolar interaction strength (J_T), and NV center concentrations (e.g., 15 ppm and 45 ppm).

**Assumptions / limitations.** Rotating wave approximation (RWA), neglecting fast-rotating terms, and assuming the driving frequency is much smaller than the zero-field splitting (Omega << D).

**Figures summary.** Fig 1 shows the experimental setup and the ZENITH pulse sequence; Fig 2 illustrates the Cayley graph construction and decoupling logic; Fig 3 compares survival probability between FID and ZENITH; Fig S2 demonstrates DC signal sensing and error metrics.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of dipolar decoherence, defines the Hamiltonian and control framework, presents the ZENITH sequence construction using group theory, validates the protocol via numerical simulations, and demonstrates its utility for DC magnetometry.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Dipolar interactions are a major source of decoherence in dense ensembles of color centers in diamond. Current protocols demand using bias magnetic fields detrimental in many scenarios. We present ZENITH (Zero-field Ensemble Neutralization via Interleaved Trilevel Handling), a pulsed sequence to cancel dipolar interactions among V-degenerate spin-1 systems. We reveal excellent coherence survival, compatibility with existing sensing sequences, and improved DC detection, advancing a general framework to control interacting degenerate multilevel systems, of broad interest in quantum technologies.

</details>

### [Single-Ensemble Multiparameter Squeezing with Qudits](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.26377v1)

**Authors:** Xiaoshui Lin, Chunlei Qu, Chong Zu, Chuanwei Zhang  
**Type:** both · **Category:** other · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.26377v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `quantum measurements` **4/5** · `Keldysh / 2PI / non-Gaussian methods` **2/5** · `entanglement & information structure` **2/5**

**Summary.** The paper shows that using qudits instead of qubits allows a single ensemble to perform simultaneous multi-parameter sensing. It establishes a mathematical framework for this effect and demonstrates significant metrological gain in a simulated trapped-ion system.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides a new route to multiparameter metrology by expanding the local Hilbert space, offering a distinct advantage over distributed architectures in the fixed-sensor-budget regime, which is highly relevant for quantum sensing and many-body dynamics.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Achieving simultaneous multiparameter sensing (e.g., vector magnetic field detection) within a single collective ensemble, which is typically limited to single-parameter metrology in qubit-based systems.

**Main result.** By promoting local sensors from qubits to qudits, the authors demonstrate that a single ensemble can support multiparameter squeezing, achieving up to 12 dB enhancement in a trapped-ion qutrit chain.

**Method.** A general framework based on the single-site Quantum Fisher Information Matrix (QFIM) to determine optimal probe states and readout observables, combined with Discrete Truncated Wigner Approximation (DTWA) for numerical simulations.

**Model / system.** A single ensemble of N identical d-level qudit sensors, specifically implemented as a trapped-ion qutrit chain with power-law interactions and a collective twisting-like interacting Hamiltonian.

**Key observables.** Multiparameter squeezing parameter (xi^2), collective spin operators (S_alpha), Symmetric Logarithmic Derivatives (SLD), and transduction-rate operator matrix (G_alpha_beta).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Local dimension (d), number of sensors (N), power-law interaction exponent (gamma), and the Standard Quantum Limit (SQL).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The ensemble is initially in a direct product state; the optimization assumes the ability to implement optimal SLD measurements; the framework is subject to the Matsumoto weak-commutativity theorem.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1(a) provides a schematic of qudits and their phase space using SU(d) generators, illustrating how multiple independent response channels can coexist.

**Paper structure.** The paper identifies the limitations of qubit-based sensing, proposes a qudit-based solution, develops a mathematical framework using QFIM, demonstrates a concrete qutrit implementation, and provides numerical evidence using a trapped-ion model.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Quantum-enhanced multiparameter sensing is often associated with distributed architectures or 2-anticoherent states, whereas squeezing in a single collective ensemble is typically limited to single-parameter metrology. Here, we show that a single ensemble can support simultaneous multiparameter squeezing when each sensor is promoted from a qubit to a qudit (i.e., spin with $d$ energy levels). We develop a general framework in which the optimal product probe state, the corresponding global readout observables, and the associated squeezing parameters are all determined from the single-site quantum Fisher information matrix. We then present a minimal qudit construction for two-parameter vector magnetic field sensing with local dimension $d=3$. We further identify a collective twisting-like interacting Hamiltonian that generates such multiparameter-squeezed states and numerically demonstrate scalable metrological gain. In particular, for a trapped-ion qutrit chain with power-law interactions, we obtain up to 12 dB enhancement in two-parameter sensing for $N=256$ sensors. Our results establish qudit-enabled multiparameter squeezing in a single ensemble as a distinct route to multiparameter quantum metrology with global readout, and highlight its potential advantage over distributed multi-ensemble strategies in the fixed-sensor-budget regime.

</details>

### [Analytical Model of Clock Drift in Quantum Key Distribution and a Simple Synchronization Algorithm](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.26705v1)

**Authors:** Loïc Millet, Boris Korzh, Rob Thew, Gianluca Boso  
**Type:** both · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.26705v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

**Summary.** This paper presents an analytical model and a practical algorithm to synchronize clocks in quantum key distribution without needing extra communication channels. By using detection timestamps to compensate for frequency mismatch, the method enables robust, long-term QKD operation even in high-loss fiber networks.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Clock frequency mismatch between transmitter and receiver in time-bin QKD causes time shifts that increase the Quantum Bit Error Rate (QBER). The goal is to develop a synchronization method that does not require a dedicated service channel or auxiliary qubit sequence.

**Main result.** The authors developed a lightweight synchronization algorithm that recovers clock drift and compensates for time offsets directly from detection timestamps, achieving stable operation over 24 hours in a metropolitan network with performance equivalent to a dedicated service channel.

**Method.** The paper uses an analytical model of clock drift and a synchronization algorithm based on the circular means of consecutive folded histograms to estimate frequency mismatch and time-offset fluctuations.

**Model / system.** A fiber-based time-bin BB84 QKD system using commercial hardware (ID Quantique Clavis XG) including gain-switched DFB lasers, modulators, and SPADs, deployed in both laboratory (100 km fiber) and field (16 km Geneva Quantum Network) settings.

**Key observables.** Quantum Bit Error Rate (QBER), photon detection-time probability distribution, clock drift rate, and Time Deviation (TDEV).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Frequency mismatch (delta f), time-bin duration (T_bin), integration time (T_int), channel loss (up to 30 dB), and detector jitter.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The frequency mismatch is assumed constant over a single integration time, and the clock drift follows a linear/aging model where the shift between consecutive acquisitions is less than half a bin width.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the experimental setup; Figure 2 illustrates the PDF of photon arrival times under different drift levels; Figure 6 demonstrates the 24-hour stability of the GQN network (drift, detection time, and QBER); Figure 7 shows the error in drift estimation with and without Poissonian noise.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of clock drift, presents an analytical model for the resulting QBER, describes the proposed synchronization algorithm, details the experimental setup and field deployment, and concludes with error analysis and stability constraints.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Clock synchronization is critical for maintaining low error rates in quantum key distribution. Here, we describe how a frequency mismatch between the transmitter and receiver clocks affects the quantum bit error rate in quantum key distribution, and derive from this model a simple synchronization algorithm together with clock stability requirements for practical operation. Our algorithm continuously compensates for both frequency mismatch and time-offset fluctuations directly from detection timestamps. It does not require a dedicated synchronization channel or auxiliary qubit sequence, converges from a large frequency mismatch within approximately one second of photon acquisition, and remains effective in low-photon-count regimes (more than 30 dB of channel loss) using standard hardware. We validate our approach by demonstrating successful key exchange over 100 km of fiber and continuous operation over 24 hours in a 16 km metropolitan network using commercial systems, with performance equivalent to using a service channel for clock synchronization.

</details>

### [Geometric Protection of Bipartite Entanglement in Hopf-Linked Quantum Rings](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.26622v1)

At extreme interlocking (β →0.01), the elimination of macroscopic spa- tial asymmetry collapses the classical level repulsion, forcing the parity gaps to converge (∆E−→∆E+) and driving the localized state E3 rapidly downward across the protected Bell manifold (red).</figcaption>

**Summary.** The study demonstrates how the non-coplanar geometry of interlocked quantum rings can protect Bell-state entanglement from Coulomb-driven decay. However, it also establishes a fundamental limit where high-order orbital transitions eventually trigger entanglement collapse. This defines the necessary conditions for achieving robust topological protection in semiconductor-based quantum architectures.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides a theoretical framework for using geometric topology and spatial symmetry to protect entanglement against many-body interactions, which is highly relevant for designing robust qubits in mesoscopic or synthetic platforms.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating the stability of bipartite entanglement (specifically Bell states) in Hopf-linked quantum rings against interaction-driven localization and parity mixing.

**Main result.** Identified a geometric protection mechanism via non-coplanar tilt that isolates the positive-parity Bell state, but discovered a critical interaction threshold (lambda_crit) beyond which higher-order transitions cause irreversible entanglement collapse.

**Method.** Exact diagonalization of the unexpanded 3D Coulomb interaction combined with a higher-order Schrieffer-Wolff transformation and symmetry analysis using a magnetic point group.

**Model / system.** Two interacting electrons confined to spatially separated, non-coplanar 1D quantum rings forming a Hopf-linked topology, subject to a local Rashba spin-orbit field and 3D Coulomb repulsion.

**Key observables.** Concurrence (C), exchange gap (Delta E+), and the interaction strength parameter (lambda).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Geometric tilt angle (alpha), interlocking parameter (beta), interaction ratio (lambda), and the dimensionless bounding constant (u_cross).

**Assumptions / limitations.** Negligible intra-band energy splittings compared to kinetic separation; use of the Heitler-London approximation for wavefunction overlap; assumes a hard-wall vacuum barrier to suppress direct tunneling.

**Figures summary.** Fig 1 shows the Hopf-linked geometry and parameters; Fig 2 illustrates the Coulomb landscape; Fig 4 shows 1D parameter slices of concurrence demonstrating entanglement protection vs. decay.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the Hopf-linked system, defines the Hamiltonian and geometric parameters, proves the spatial symmetry for protection, applies Schrieffer-Wolff to find the collapse threshold, and discusses implementation constraints in semiconductor architectures.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

We determine the bipartite entanglement bounds of two interacting electrons in deeply interlocked Hopf-linked quantum rings via exact diagonalization of the unexpanded 3D Coulomb interaction. This identifies an exact continuous spatial symmetry that geometrically isolates the positive-parity Bell state, preventing classical interaction-driven localization. A non-coplanar geometric tilt ($α> 0$) is essential to lift the exchange degeneracy and maintain this maximally entangled manifold as a state of frozen entanglement. However, a higher-order Schrieffer-Wolff transformation demonstrates this geometric protection is fundamentally bounded; uncancelled inter-orbital momentum transitions inevitably induce dynamical parity mixing. This defines a critical interaction threshold ($λ_{crit}$) for irreversible entanglement collapse. Our analysis shows that the resulting bounding conditions reveal scaling limitations in mesoscopic semiconductor architectures, dictating the necessity of synthetic macroscopic platforms to achieve robust topological protection.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2605.26226"></a>
### [Hydrodynamic Cooperons in Electron Fluids: Schwinger--Keldysh Derivation and Quantum Corrections to Magnetoresistance](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.26226v1)

**Authors:** Alberto Cortijo  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** strongly correlated electrons · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.26226v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `Keldysh / 2PI / non-Gaussian methods` **4/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **2/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.26226_figures/2605.26226_fig1.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> FIG. 1: Hydrodynamic harmonic hierarchy and stress-sector closure. The density mode m = 0 and momentum modes m = ±1 are coupled by gradients and are protected by conservation laws, while the first nonconserved sector (represented by the dashed boxes) is the spin-two stress mode m = ±2. In the bare hydrodynamic closure, integrating out the stress sector generates the viscosity ν0. In the quantum-corrected theory, the hydrodynamic Cooperon renormalizes the stress relaxation rate, Γπ →Γπ + δΓ2, with Γπ the bare spin-two relaxation rate, which feeds back into the momentum sector as an effective viscosity νeff.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">

(a) In the clean hydrodynamic regime, a uniform driving field E produces a smooth electron-fluid velocity profile u(r) in a channel with no-slip boundaries. (b) In the presence of static inhomogeneous random friction, described by a spatially varying field ζ(r), the local drag force fdrag(r) = −ζ(r) u(r) opposes the flow and distorts the velocity streamlines. The color map represents the spatial variation of the friction strength, with stronger-friction regions producing a larger local suppression of the flow. This disorder realization provides the minimal hydrodynamic mechanism used in the Schwinger–Keldysh treatment to generate...</figcaption>
</figure>

The bubble ΠRA(Ω, Q) is built from one retarded and one advanced transverse hydrodynamic propagator. The second term contains one explicit disorder insertion; the Cooperon box on the right represents the remaining resummed ladder.</figcaption>

<img src="2605.26226_figures/2605.26226_fig4.jpg" alt="Figure 4">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 4.</b> FIG. 4: Representative magnetoviscous response including the hydrodynamic-Cooperon stress correction. (a) Channel magnetoresistance ρch(B) at fixed temperature. The dashed black curve is the semiclassical result obtained from the bare stress relaxation rate Γπ(T), while the blue curve includes the Cooperon-induced correction Γπ →Γπ + δΓ2(T, B). The quantum-corrected curve (solid blue line) develops a narrow low-field dip because the Cooperon correction is largest at B = 0 and is suppressed by orbital magnetic dephasing at small finite field, while the broader background is controlled by the semiclassical magnetoviscous response (black dashed–dotted curve). <figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 5.</b> FIG. 5: Quantum correction to the Hall-viscous component of the magnetoviscosity tensor. (a) Semiclassical (black dashed curve) and quantum-corrected (blue solid curve) Hall viscosities as a function of magnetic field. The Cooperon correction preserves the odd-in-B symmetry of νxy, but suppresses the low-field slope through Γπ →Γπ + δΓ2(B, T). (b) Temperature dependence of νxy at two representative values of the magnetic field, blue B = 0.03T and orange B = 0.12T. In both cases the strong reduction of the quantum-corrected Hall viscosity with increasing temperature reflects the thermal dephasing effect of the hydrodynamic Cooperon in presence of magnetic fields.</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** The paper derives a theory for quantum interference effects in electron fluids, specifically identifying a 'hydrodynamic Cooperon' that modifies stress relaxation. This mechanism predicts unique signatures in the magnetoresistance and Hall viscosity of high-mobility 2D electron gases, distinguishing quantum corrections from classical magnetohydrodynamic effects.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Developing a consistent Schwinger-Keldysh effective theory for quantum-interference corrections (hydrodynamic Cooperons) in the hydrodynamic regime of 2D electron systems and determining their impact on transport properties.

**Main result.** The theory shows that the hydrodynamic Cooperon renormalizes the spin-two stress sector, leading to a reduction in effective shear viscosity and a characteristic low-field magnetoresistance dip/shoulder.

**Method.** Real-time Schwinger-Keldysh field theory combined with a diagrammatic ladder resummation (Bethe-Salpeter equation) and the self-consistent Born approximation.

**Model / system.** A two-dimensional electron system in the hydrodynamic regime (high-mobility conductors) subject to a minimal random-friction disorder model that introduces momentum relaxation.

**Key observables.** Shear viscosity, longitudinal and Hall viscosities, channel magnetoresistance, and stress relaxation rate.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Momentum-relaxation time (tau_mc), cyclotron frequency (omega_c), shear viscosity (nu), and the hydrodynamic ultraviolet cutoff (Lambda).

**Assumptions / limitations.** Weak-damping/weak-relaxation limit, truncation of the angular harmonic hierarchy to m=0, +/-1, and +/-2, and the use of a sharp hydrodynamic momentum cutoff.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 depicts the harmonic hierarchy of modes; Figure 4 shows the predicted low-field magnetoresistance dip and nonmonotonic temperature dependence; Figure 5 illustrates the Hall-viscosity kink and its temperature dependence.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the hydrodynamic problem, develops the Schwinger-Keldysh framework with a random-friction disorder model, derives the Cooperon pole and its renormalization of the stress sector, analyzes the effect of a magnetic field (orbital dephasing and viscosity modification), and concludes by identifying experimental signatures in magnetoresistance and Hall viscosity.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

We develop a Schwinger--Keldysh effective theory for quantum-interference corrections in a two-dimensional electron system in the hydrodynamic regime. Starting from the clean hydrodynamic fixed point, we introduce a minimal random-friction disorder model that generates a finite momentum-relaxation time within the self-consistent Born approximation. The disorder-averaged theory then allows us to construct a hydrodynamic Cooperon and to compute the associated self-energy corrections to the collective modes. Conservation laws protect the density and momentum sectors, so that the leading quantum-coherence correction is forced into the spin-two stress sector. The associated stress self-energy renormalizes the shear viscosity and modifies both the Gurzhi response and its low-field magnetohydrodynamic signatures.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2605.26272"></a>
### [Kubo-Ando Means and Rigidity of Quantum Positivity Cones](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.26272v1)

**Authors:** Mohsen Kian  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.26272v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `entanglement & information structure` **4/5** · `methods for driven-dissipative` **2/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.26272_figures/2605.26272_page2.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 2</figcaption>

<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.26272_figures/2605.26272_page4.jpg" alt="Figure 3">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 3.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 4</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.26272_figures/2605.26272_page5.jpg" alt="Figure 4">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 4.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 5</figcaption>

<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.26272_figures/2605.26272_page6.jpg" alt="Figure 5">

**Summary.** This paper demonstrates that only standard convex mixing (arithmetic means) preserves the essential entanglement-related properties of quantum states and channels. It shows that any other type of Kubo-Ando averaging can destroy separability or increase the complexity of entanglement (Schmidt number).

**Why it may be interesting.** This is highly relevant for researchers in open quantum systems and quantum information, as it establishes fundamental limits on how non-linear averaging processes can affect entanglement and the structural integrity of quantum channels.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper investigates the stability and rigidity of quantum positivity cones (separable, PPT, and Schmidt-number cones) under the action of nonlinear Kubo-Ando operator means.

**Main result.** The authors prove that weighted arithmetic means are the only Kubo-Ando means that preserve the separable cone and the class of entanglement-breaking channels; all other means can increase Schmidt numbers or violate the PPT condition.

**Method.** The study uses curvature analysis of operator monotone functions, Taylor expansions, and the construction of explicit two-qubit counterexamples, extended to higher dimensions via canonical isometries and the Choi-Jamiołkowski correspondence.

**Model / system.** The mathematical framework involves bipartite tensor product spaces (C^m tensor C^n) and the study of operator means acting on positive operators and quantum channels.

**Key observables.** Schmidt number, PPT (positive partial transpose) property, and separability.

**Important parameters / regimes.** The curvature of the operator monotone function (kappa_sigma), where kappa_sigma = 0 corresponds to arithmetic means and kappa_sigma > 0 corresponds to non-arithmetic means.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The results specifically address the behavior of non-arithmetic Kubo-Ando means and assume the use of the Choi-Jamiołkowski correspondence to relate operators to maps.

**Paper structure.** The paper begins by defining the curvature of Kubo-Ando means, moves to proving rigidity theorems for separable and PPT cones using two-qubit counterexamples, extends these results to Schmidt-number cones, and concludes by translating these findings to the theory of quantum channels.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

We investigate the stability of quantum positivity cones under nonlinear operator means. Specifically, we examine how Kubo--Ando means interact with the separable, positive partial transpose (PPT), and Schmidt-number cones. By analyzing the curvature of operator monotone functions at the identity, we give a strict rigidity phenomenon: weighted arithmetic means are the only Kubo--Ando means that preserve the separable cone in all dimensions. We show that the strictly positive curvature of any non-arithmetic mean explicitly forces a violation of the PPT condition, even in the foundational two-qubit setting, and can strictly increase the Schmidt number of the resulting operator. Finally, using the Choi--Jamiołkowski correspondence, we translate these geometric obstructions to the map-theoretic setting, concluding that convex mixing is the uniquely permissible Kubo--Ando operation for preserving entanglement-breaking quantum channels.

</details>

### [Practical Entanglement Distillation Protocols with Quadratic Error Suppression](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.26757v1)

**Authors:** Elisa Bäumer Marty  
**Type:** both · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.26757v1>

(d) Two recurrence rounds (here Z and X) detect any single error. (e) Maneva-Smolin protocol, which increases the output rate by checking multiple Bell pairs jointly. (f) Leung-Shor protocol, which outputs two Bell pairs with quadratic error suppression.</figcaption>

The protocol accepts if c1 = c2 and c3 = c4, and in (a) additionally requires c3 = c4 = 0. (a) Space-optimal protocol with quadratic suppression of any two-qubit Pauli errors. (b) Reduced space-optimal protocol with fewer gates, achieving quadratic suppression only for arbitrary single-qubit Pauli errors. (c) High-rate protocol acting on m qubits per module and outputting m −2 Bell pairs with quadratic error suppression.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.26757_figures/2605.26757_fig3.jpg" alt="Figure 3">

In (a), (c) and (e) we consider only single-qubit depolarizing errors, while in (b), (d) and (f) we consider uniform two-qubit depolarizing errors.</figcaption>
</figure>

<img src="2605.26757_figures/2605.26757_fig4.jpg" alt="Figure 4">

(c) The total and normalized duration of the protocols when compiled on ibm pittsburgh as a function of the number of Bell pairs that are produced. Note that the single-recurrence protocol corresponds to the Maneva-Smolin protocol with one output Bell pair and similarly the Leung-Shor protocol corresponds to the high-rate protocol with two output Bell pairs.</figcaption>

</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** This paper introduces new, highly efficient entanglement distillation protocols designed for modular quantum computing. By using inter-module gates as active components, the proposed protocols achieve quadratic error suppression using only two qubits per module, making them practical for near-term hardware.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Inter-module operations in modular quantum computing architectures exhibit much higher error rates than local operations, creating a bottleneck for scaling. Existing entanglement distillation protocols are often too resource-intensive in terms of qubits and time for near-term hardware.

**Main result.** The authors developed a space-optimal distillation protocol requiring only two qubits per module that achieves quadratic error suppression of inter-module errors. This protocol outperforms existing small-scale protocols in both simulations and experiments on superconducting hardware.

**Method.** The study uses a generalized resource model where inter-module entangling operations are used actively during the protocol. The researchers compared new protocols against established ones using numerical simulations and experimental implementation on the IBM pittsburgh processor.

**Model / system.** The system is a modular quantum computing architecture, specifically implemented and tested on the IBM pittsburgh superconducting quantum processor. The noise model uses a stochastic Pauli channel with single-qubit and two-qubit correlated errors.

**Key observables.** Bell-state fidelity, normalized error, output error rate, and protocol duration (depth and wall-clock time).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Inter-module error rate (epsilon_inter), local error rates, qubit count per module, and gate durations (e.g., 88 ns for CZ, 32 ns for single-qubit gates).

**Assumptions / limitations.** Local operations and measurements are assumed to be significantly more reliable than inter-module operations; the low-error regime is the primary focus.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows existing recurrence and large-scale protocols; Figure 2 illustrates the new space-optimal and high-rate protocols; Figure 3 shows simulations of output error vs. inter-module error; Figure 4 presents experimental results comparing error suppression and protocol duration on IBM hardware; Figure 5 shows the device layout and hardware noise statistics.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the bottleneck of inter-module errors, proposes new space-efficient distillation protocols, provides analytical error suppression analysis, compares these protocols to existing methods via simulation, and validates the results through experiments on a superconducting processor.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Near-term and early fault-tolerant quantum computing architectures are expected to exhibit highly non-uniform error rates. In particular, local operations within a chip can be substantially more reliable than operations connecting different chips or dilution refrigerators. Such inter-module operations can therefore become a dominant bottleneck, even when quantum error correction is applied. Entanglement distillation provides a natural way to trade additional operations and qubits for higher-fidelity entanglement. Standard distillation protocols, however, are usually formulated in an LOCC resource model, in which several noisy Bell pairs are generated initially and all subsequent processing consists only of local operations and classical communication. Here, we consider a generalized model tailored to modular quantum computing hardware, in which the two modules have access to high-fidelity local operations and to repeated uses of the same noisy inter-module entangling operation during the protocol. We develop practical small-scale entanglement distillation protocols designed to minimize both space and time overhead. Remarkably, our main protocol requires only two qubits per module, yet achieves quadratic error suppression of inter-module errors, assuming local operations are much cleaner. Compared with existing small-scale protocols, our space-optimal protocol provides more space- and time-efficient quadratic error suppression and achieves the best performance in our simulations and experiments on noisy links of current superconducting quantum processors. These results suggest that inter-module-gate-assisted entanglement distillation can be a practical primitive for overcoming noisy links in modular quantum computing architectures.

</details>

**Summary.** This paper introduces a new self-consistent method for calculating many-body Green functions using spectral quadrature. By using an SVD-based criterion to select the optimal number of poles, the approach captures essential strongly correlated physics, such as the Mott transition and Kondo resonance, more accurately than traditional one-shot methods.

**Why it may be interesting.** The method provides a non-perturbative, numerically stable way to reconstruct spectral functions and capture complex many-body features like Kondo resonances and Mott transitions without the need for external terminators or diagrammatic expansions.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The difficulty of calculating many-body Green functions for strongly correlated systems where standard power-series expansions fail to capture non-perturbative phenomena like the Mott transition or Kondo resonance.

**Main result.** The development of a self-consistent spectral quadrature (sc-SQ) framework that accurately captures the three-peak structure of the Anderson impurity model and the Mott gap formation in the Hubbard model, with results qualitatively agreeing with NRG.

**Method.** A self-consistent framework using Gauss-Christoffel quadrature to approximate the Kallen-Lehmann spectral measure, utilizing an SVD-based rank-selection criterion to identify the numerically resolvable pole rank.

**Model / system.** The method is benchmarked using the Anderson Impurity Model (AIM) and the Hubbard model on a Bethe lattice within the Dynamical Mean-Field Theory (DMFT) framework.

**Key observables.** Spectral function A(omega), spectral moments, quasiparticle weight (Z), occupancy, and self-energy.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Interaction strength (U), bandwidth (D), hybridization (Gamma), and the quadrature pole order (N).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The accuracy is limited by the number of resolvable spectral moments and the numerical precision of the input moments; the method relies on the ability to resolve the singular-value gap in the Hankel matrix.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 compares sc-SQ variants against NRG for the AIM and shows the SVD spectrum; Figure 2 compares one-shot vs. self-consistent approaches in the mixed-valence regime; Figure 3 shows the improvement in spectral resolution as N increases; Figure 4 illustrates the Mott transition and quasiparticle weight.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the sc-SQ framework, establishes mathematical equivalences between quadrature, Padé approximants, and continued fractions, details the SVD-based stabilization and self-consistency algorithm, and concludes with benchmarks against NRG for the Anderson and Hubbard models.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

We develop a self-consistent spectral quadrature (sc-SQ) framework for the calculation of many-body Green functions. The method approximates the Källén--Lehmann spectral measure by Gauss--Christoffel (GC) quadrature, yielding a rational Green function representation with guaranteed spectral positivity that exactly reproduces the first $2N$ spectral moments at pole order $N$. A key component is an SVD-based rank-selection criterion on the Hankel matrix, which identifies the numerically resolvable pole rank $N^*$ from the singular-value gap and acts as a precision-guided diagnostic of correlation complexity. The scheme is made self-consistent by requiring that the spectral function used to evaluate expectation values coincides with the spectral function generated by the quadrature reconstruction. This defines a fixed-point hierarchy that connects systematically to established approximations, including Hartree--Fock and Hubbard-I, and incorporates non-perturbative features such as multi-peak spectral structure. We benchmark the approach for the Anderson impurity model against numerical renormalization group (NRG) results and apply it within dynamical mean-field theory for the Hubbard model on the Bethe lattice. The method captures the three-peak Anderson impurity spectrum and the suppression of quasiparticle weight in the half-filled Hubbard model on the Bethe lattice, including Mott-gap formation on the insulating branch for $N\geqslant 5$, in qualitative agreement with NRG references.

</details>

<a id="paper-2605.26925"></a>
### [Adaptive Reinforcement Learning for Robust Open Quantum System Control: A Multi-Task Framework with Temporal Optimization](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.26925v1)

**Authors:** Haftu W. Fentaw, Steve Campbell, Simon Caton  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.26925v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `methods for driven-dissipative` **4/5**

**Summary.** The paper presents a multi-task reinforcement learning framework that learns to control various quantum systems simultaneously. By optimizing both the control pulses and the timing parameters, the method achieves high-fidelity state transfer and outperforms traditional gradient-based methods in robustness against environmental noise.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work is highly relevant for researchers in open quantum systems as it provides a scalable, machine-learning-based approach to achieving universal control that is inherently robust to the types of noise and parameter drift encountered in realistic quantum hardware.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Developing a robust, unified quantum control framework that generalizes across diverse Hamiltonians and maintains high fidelity in the presence of environmental noise and hardware uncertainties.

**Main result.** A multi-task Soft Actor-Critic (SAC) reinforcement learning agent achieves high-fidelity state transfer across 51 different Hamiltonians and demonstrates superior robustness to pulse amplitude and decoherence fluctuations compared to the GRAPE algorithm.

**Method.** A multi-task Soft Actor-Critic (SAC) reinforcement learning framework that uses a system descriptor to condition the policy and simultaneously optimizes control pulse amplitudes, total evolution time (T), and the number of pulse segments (N).

**Model / system.** Open quantum systems ranging from single-qubit to three-qupi configurations, modeled using the Lindblad master equation to account for amplitude damping and dephasing noise.

**Key observables.** State transfer fidelity (F) and the Robustness Infidelity Measure (RIM) based on the Wasserstein distance.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Evolution time (T), number of pulse segments (N), decoherence rate (gamma), and pulse amplitude perturbations.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The system is prepared in a pure initial state; decoherence is primarily modeled via amplitude damping; the use of Born-Markov and Secular approximations for the Lindblad equation.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 compares closed-system fidelities between task-specific and multi-task models; Figure 2 shows open-system fidelity distributions; Figure 3 compares the RIM of SAC versus GRAPE; Figure 4 shows the learned distributions of temporal parameters T and N.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of robust control, describes the multi-task SAC architecture and adaptive temporal optimization, details the training strategy via progressive Hamiltonian expansion, presents benchmarks for closed and open systems, and concludes with a robustness analysis and discussion of scalability.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

We present a Multi-task Soft Actor-Critic (SAC) Reinforcement Learning framework designed for open-system quantum control across diverse Hamiltonians, which learns optimal pulse sequences while simultaneously discovering problem-specific evolution time T and number of control pulse segments N. Experimental results across 51 Hamiltonian variations demonstrate that the multi-task SAC model is able to generate control pulses that can drive a system, under environment noise, from its initial state to its target state with high fidelities, establishing essential foundations for universal quantum control applicable to realistic noisy quantum devices. Through progressive expansion of the training Hamiltonian set, we investigate if a single multi-task model trained using a given number of sample Hamiltonians can successfully accomplish state-transfer tasks for Hamiltonians drawn from the same Hamiltonian space but not encountered during training. In addition, our Robustness Infidelity Measure (RIM) analysis reveals that SAC trained policies exhibit superior robustness to pulse amplitude perturbations and decoherence rate variations compared to GRAPE-optimized controls.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2605.26866"></a>
### [Encrypted Cloning, Absolute Maximal Entanglement and Quantum Secret Sharing](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.26866v1)

**Authors:** Zheng Liang Lim, Hoi-Kwong Lo  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.26866v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `entanglement & information structure` **4/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.26866_figures/2605.26866_fig1.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> FIG. 1. A schematic diagram of the partial encrypted cloning protocol for n = 2, d = 2. The machine for en- crypted cloning contains the signal qubits and the qubit from register A2. They are the states affected by the encryption operator. The key box contains the noise qubits, which are decryption keys. The group of states, containing A2, S1, S2, N1, N2 forms a AME(5, 2) state. The overall state with A1 forms the AME(6, 2) state. The brown dotted lines show an example of an autho- rised set: {S1, N1, N2}. The purple dotted lines show an example of an unauthorised set: {A2, S2}. The size of the authorised set is 3, and that of the unauthorised set is 2, thus illustrating a QSS ((3, 5))...</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** This paper generalizes the qubit-based encrypted cloning protocol to arbitrary dimensions using Weyl-Heisenberg operators. It proves that this protocol is fundamentally linked to the construction of five-party AME states and threshold quantum secret sharing schemes. The results show that the protocol is robust against the loss of certain noise keys, provided appropriate replacements are used.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work provides a deep algebraic connection between quantum communication protocols (cloning and secret sharing) and the fundamental structure of multipartite entanglement (AME states), which is highly relevant to quantum error correction and distributed quantum computing.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper aims to generalize the 'encrypted cloning' protocol from qubits to arbitrary dimensions (qudits) and formally establish its relationship with Quantum Secret Sharing (QSS) and Absolutely Maximally Entangled (AME) states.

**Main result.** The authors prove that an encrypted qudit system with two signal-noise pairs is equivalent to a five-party AME state and demonstrate that encrypted cloning is a specific instance of a threshold QSS scheme.

**Method.** The authors use a framework based on Weyl-Heisenberg displacement operators and the Choi-Jamiolkowski isomorphism to analytically derive the encrypted state and verify its entanglement properties.

**Model / system.** A multipartite quantum system consisting of an input target qudit, $n$ pairs of maximally entangled signal-noise qudits, and a global encryption unitary based on generalized Pauli operators.

**Key observables.** Reduced density matrices of various subsystems (to check for maximal mixing), Schmidt rank, and the unitarity of the encryption/decryption operators.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Dimension $d$ of the Hilbert space, number of signal-noise pairs $n$, and the specific quadratic phase factor $\phi(a, b)$ used in the Weyl-Heisenberg construction.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The equivalence to AME states holds provided the input state is uniform; the protocol assumes access to the noise qudits as decryption keys.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 provides a schematic of the $n=2, d=2$ partial encrypted cloning protocol, illustrating the roles of the 'Key box' (noise qubits) and the 'Machine' (signal and auxiliary qubits) in a threshold QSS scheme.

**Paper structure.** The paper begins by introducing the problem of generalization, develops a Weyl-Heisenberg framework for arbitrary dimensions, proves the AME correspondence for $n=2$, establishes the formal link to QSS, and concludes with error/loss analysis and limitations.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

The no-cloning theorem prohibits the creation of identical copies of quantum information, imposing fundamental constraints on quantum technologies. A recently proposed protocol, encrypted cloning, introduced by Yamaguchi and Kempf, showed that perfect qubit clones can be produced if they are simultaneously encrypted with a single-use key. They also observed a connection between this scheme and quantum secret sharing (QSS). However, it remained an open question whether encrypted cloning could be generalised to arbitrary dimensions, and the broader relationship between the two schemes had not been formally established. In this work, we address both questions by framing encrypted clones as Absolutely Maximally Entangled (AME) states. In parallel with recent work by Ceará that utilises Zadoff-Chu sequences, we independently develop a complementary framework for arbitrary dimensions based on Weyl-Heisenberg displacement operators, both tracing back to the original qubit construction by Yamaguchi and Kempf. We analytically compute the encrypted state and prove that an encrypted qudit system comprising two signal-noise qudit pairs is equivalent to a five-party AME state in any dimension, provided the input state is uniform. We then formalise the connection to QSS by proving that a threshold QSS scheme can achieve the fundamental objectives of encrypted cloning, establishing QSS as the natural general framework within which encrypted cloning can be contextualised.

</details>

<a id="paper-2605.26920"></a>
### [Extremal Marginal States of Maximal Rank in $(d, d+m)$](http://arxiv.org/abs/2605.26920v1)

**Authors:** Indu Bala, Swapan Rana  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2605.26920v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `entanglement & information structure` **4/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.26920_figures/2605.26920_page2.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 2</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">

<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 3.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 4</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.26920_figures/2605.26920_page5.jpg" alt="Figure 4">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 4.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 5</figcaption>

<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2605.26920_figures/2605.26920_page6.jpg" alt="Figure 5">
